## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science and solid mechanics
**Analysis**: The variables stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T) define constitutive relationships governing material deformation. Temperature typically modulates elastic modulus, yield strength, and hardening behavior, leading to coupled thermo-mechanical models that capture phenomena like thermal softening, plastic flow, and thermoelastic expansion.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress accounting for thermal expansion strain)
- Temperature-modified Hooke's law: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus)
- Voce-type hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturation hardening coupled with exponential thermal effects)
- Power-law thermo-plasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (nonlinear stress-strain scaling modulated by temperature)
- Johnson-Cook simplified form: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T) (empirical plasticity with linear thermal degradation)
- Eyring thermal activation model: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (stress-driven dislocation motion with temperature-dependent activation)
- Ramberg-Osgood approximation: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * epsilon**c2) (nonlinear elastic-plastic transition curve)
- Thermo-viscoelastic relaxation: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(-c1 * T) + c2 * (1 - exp(-c3 * epsilon)) (combined thermal decay and strain hardening)
- Polynomial thermo-mechanical coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T (multivariate expansion for coupled thermal-strain effects)
- Threshold-yield with thermal shift: sigma = Max(0, c0 * (epsilon - c1) - c2 * T) (perfectly plastic behavior with temperature-dependent yield threshold)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic-perfectly plastic transition → Piecewise linear switching or Min(c1*epsilon, c2) structure
- Thermal softening of yield strength → Multiplicative temperature decay factor (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) scaling the strain-dependent term
- Dislocation strain hardening → Concave power-law or logarithmic increase with strain epsilon**c (0<c<1) or log(c + epsilon)
- Thermoelastic strain compensation → Linear subtraction of thermal expansion term (epsilon - c*T) prior to modulus multiplication
- Ductile-to-brittle transition → Sharp slope change modulated by tanh(c*(T - c_ref)) or arctan(c*T)
- Creep-assisted deformation → Exponential temperature activation exp(c*T) multiplying strain or stress terms
- Anelastic recovery and cyclic softening → Asymmetric nonlinear terms or sign-dependent functions like sgn(epsilon)*Abs(epsilon)**c

The user wants me to identify which candidates are mathematically equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT).

**Ground Truth (GT):**
`c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*(T - c3)*sin(epsilon)`
Numerical values:
`c0 = 5.889184448896621`
`c1 = 3.0`
`c2 = 2.8821771197066277`
`c3 = 279.6235977851866`
So, GT = `5.889184448896621 * epsilon**3 + 2.8821771197066277 * (T - 279.6235977851866) * sin(epsilon)`
Let's rewrite GT in a more general form to match candidates:
`A * epsilon**3 + B * T * sin(epsilon) + C * sin(epsilon)`
where `A = c0`, `B = c2`, `C = -c2 * c3`.
So GT is a linear combination of `epsilon**3`, `T * sin(epsilon)`, and `sin(epsilon)`.
Actually, `c2*(T - c3)*sin(epsilon) = c2*T*sin(epsilon) - c2*c3*sin(epsilon)`.
So the basis functions are `epsilon**3`, `T*sin(epsilon)`, and `sin(epsilon)`.
Wait, `sin(epsilon)` and `T*sin(epsilon)` can be combined if we allow constants to depend on T, but T is a variable. So we need terms that can produce `epsilon**3`, `T*sin(epsilon)`, and `sin(epsilon)`.
Or simply: `c_a * epsilon**3 + c_b * T * sin(epsilon) + c_d * sin(epsilon)`.

Let's check the candidates. Many candidates have the form:
`T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + ...`
Let's expand `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2)`:
`T * c0 * (sin(c1*epsilon)*cos(c2) + cos(c1*epsilon)*sin(c2))`
`= T * (c0*cos(c2)) * sin(c1*epsilon) + T * (c0*sin(c2)) * cos(c1*epsilon)`
To match `B * T * sin(epsilon)`, we need `c1 = 1` (or -1, but sin is odd, so sign can be absorbed), and `cos(c2) = 1` => `c2 = 0` (or multiple of 2pi). Then the term becomes `T * c0 * sin(epsilon)`.
So candidates with `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2)` can match `T * sin(epsilon)` if `c1=1, c2=0`.
The remaining part of GT is `A * epsilon**3 + C * sin(epsilon)`.
So we need a candidate that can produce `epsilon**3` and `sin(epsilon)` (without T) from its other terms.
Many candidates have `+ c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + ...`
If `c4=0`, we get `epsilon**3`.
But we also need a standalone `sin(epsilon)` term (coefficient `C`).
Does any candidate have a standalone `sin(epsilon)` or something that can become it?
Let's look at Candidate 1: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*cos(c6*exp(c7*epsilon))`
Can `c5*cos(...)` become `sin(epsilon)`? No.
Can `c4*epsilon` become `sin(epsilon)`? No.
So Candidate 1 lacks a standalone `sin(epsilon)` term. Wait, `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2)` expands to `T * (...) * sin(epsilon) + T * (...) * cos(epsilon)`. It has T in it. It cannot produce a standalone `sin(epsilon)` term unless T is constant, but T is a variable.
Wait, look at Candidate 18: `T*c0*sin(c1 + epsilon) + c2*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon + c4*sin(c5 + c6*epsilon)`
Here, `c4*sin(c5 + c6*epsilon)` can be `C * sin(epsilon)` if `c6=1, c5=0`.
And `T*c0*sin(c1 + epsilon)` can be `B * T * sin(epsilon)` if `c1=0`.
And `c2*epsilon**3` matches `A * epsilon**3`.
`c3*epsilon` can be set to 0.
So Candidate 18 looks promising.
Let's check Candidate 18 carefully:
`T*c0*sin(c1 + epsilon) + c2*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon + c4*sin(c5 + c6*epsilon)`
Set `c1 = 0` => `T*c0*sin(epsilon)`
Set `c6 = 1, c5 = 0` => `c4*sin(epsilon)`
Set `c3 = 0`
Then it becomes `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c2*epsilon**3 + c4*sin(epsilon)`
This matches `B*T*sin(epsilon) + A*epsilon**3 + C*sin(epsilon)`.
So Candidate 18 is a MATCH.

Let's check other candidates with similar structure.
Candidate 9: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*exp(T*c6)*sin(c7*epsilon + c8)`

Let's systematically go through all candidates.
GT structure: `A * epsilon**3 + B * T * sin(epsilon) + C * sin(epsilon)`
We need candidates that can form these three terms.
Note: `sin(epsilon)` and `T*sin(epsilon)` are linearly independent with respect to T.
So we need terms that can produce `epsilon**3`, `T*sin(epsilon)`, and `sin(epsilon)`.
Or maybe `T*sin(epsilon + phase)` and `sin(epsilon + phase)` can cover it.

Let's list candidates that have `epsilon**3` and `sin` terms.
1: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*cos(...)` -> No standalone sin.
2: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon + ...` -> No epsilon**3.
3: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*log(...)` -> No standalone sin.
4: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon + ...` -> No epsilon**3.
5: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon + ...` -> No epsilon**3.
6: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*exp(...)` -> No standalone sin.
7: `(c0*epsilon + c1 + (c2*epsilon + c3)*(T*c4*sin(c5*epsilon + c6) + c7*epsilon + c8*asinh(c9*epsilon)))/(c2*epsilon + c3)`
Simplifies to `c0*epsilon/(c2*epsilon+c3) + c1/(c2*epsilon+c3) + T*c4*sin(...) + c7*epsilon + c8*asinh(...)`.
Has `T*sin(...)`, but no `epsilon**3`. NO MATCH.
8: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon + ...` -> No epsilon**3.
9: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*exp(T*c6)*sin(c7*epsilon + c8)`
As analyzed, if `c6=0`, `exp(T*c6)=1`. Then `c5*sin(c7*epsilon+c8)` can be `C*sin(epsilon)`.
`T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon+c2)` can be `B*T*sin(epsilon)`.
`c3*epsilon**3` matches `A*epsilon**3`.
`c4*epsilon` can be 0.
So Candidate 9 is a MATCH.

10: `c0*cos(...) + c2*exp(...) + c4*sin(...)` -> No T, no epsilon**3.
11: `c0*(c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*(c4*cos(...) + c6*exp(...)))` -> No T, no epsilon**3.
12: `c0*cos(...) + c2*exp(...) + c4*epsilon + c5` -> No T, no epsilon**3.
13: `c0*cos(...) + c2*epsilon**2 + c3*exp(...) + c5*epsilon` -> No T, no epsilon**3.
14: `c0*cos(...) + c2*exp(...) + c4*exp(...) + c6` -> No T, no epsilon**3.
15: `(c0*epsilon + c1 + (T*c2 + c3)*(T*c4*sin(c5*epsilon + c6) + c7*epsilon + c8*asinh(c9*epsilon)))/(T*c2 + c3)`
Simplifies to `c0*epsilon/(T*c2+c3) + c1/(T*c2+c3) + T*c4*sin(...) + c7*epsilon + c8*asinh(...)`.
No epsilon**3. NO MATCH.
16: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon + c4*log(...)` -> No epsilon**3.
17: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon + c4*asinh(...) + c6*sin(c7 + c8*epsilon)`
Has `T*sin(...)`, `sin(...)`, but no `epsilon**3`. NO MATCH.
18: `T*c0*sin(c1 + epsilon) + c2*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon + c4*sin(c5 + c6*epsilon)`
Matches as analyzed. MATCH.
19: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon + c4*asinh(...) + c6*exp(c7/T)` -> No epsilon**3.
20: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon) + c2*epsilon + c3*exp(c4*epsilon)*sin(T*c5 + c6)` -> No epsilon**3.
21: `(c0*epsilon + c1 + (T*c2 + c3)*(T*c4*sin(c5 + epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon))/(T*c2 + c3)`
Simplifies to `c0*epsilon/(T*c2+c3) + c1/(T*c2+c3) + T*c4*sin(c5+epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon`.
Has `T*sin(...)`, `epsilon**3`, but no standalone `sin(epsilon)`. The `sin` term is multiplied by T.
Wait, GT has `c2*(T - c3)*sin(epsilon) = c2*T*sin(epsilon) - c2*c3*sin(epsilon)`.
So we need a standalone `sin(epsilon)` term. Candidate 21 lacks it. NO MATCH.
22: `T*c0*sin(c1 + epsilon) + T*c2 + c3*epsilon + c4*asinh(c5*epsilon) + c6` -> No epsilon**3.
23: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*sin(c6*log(T*c7 + 1) + c8)` -> sin depends on T. NO MATCH.
24: `(c0*epsilon + c1 + (c2*epsilon + c3)*(T*c4*sin(c5 + epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon))/(c2*epsilon + c3)`
Simplifies to `c0*epsilon/(c2*epsilon+c3) + c1/(c2*epsilon+c3) + T*c4*sin(c5+epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon`.
No standalone sin. NO MATCH.
25: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon + c4*sin(c5*exp(c6*epsilon) + c7)` -> No epsilon**3.
26: `(T*c0 + c1 + (c2*epsilon + c3)*(T*c4*sin(c5*epsilon + c6) + c7*epsilon + c8*asinh(c9*epsilon)))/(c2*epsilon + c3)`
Simplifies to `T*c0/(c2*epsilon+c3) + c1/(c2*epsilon+c3) + T*c4*sin(...) + c7*epsilon + c8*asinh(...)`.
No epsilon**3. NO MATCH.
27: `(T*c0 + c1 + (c2*epsilon + c3)*(T*c4*sin(c5 + epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon))/(c2*epsilon + c3)`
Simplifies to `T*c0/(c2*epsilon+c3) + c1/(c2*epsilon+c3) + T*c4*sin(c5+epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon`.
No standalone sin. NO MATCH.
28: `(T*c0 + c1 + (T*c2 + c3)*(T*c4*sin(c5 + epsilon) + c6*epsilon + c7*asinh(c8*epsilon)))/(T*c2 + c3)`
Simplifies to `T*c0/(T*c2+c3) + c1/(T*c2+c3) + T*c4*sin(c5+epsilon) + c6*epsilon + c7*asinh(...)`.
No epsilon**3. NO MATCH.
29: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon + c4*(c5*exp(c6*epsilon) + 1)*exp(T*c7)` -> No epsilon**3.
30: `c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**2 + c2*exp(c3*epsilon) + c4*epsilon*exp(T*c5) + c6 + c7*epsilon**4/sqrt(T)` -> No sin.
31: `c0*log(c1*epsilon + 1)*sin(T*c2 + c3) + epsilon*(T*c4 + c5)` -> No epsilon**3.
32: `T*c0*sin(...) + c3*epsilon + c4*asinh(...) + c6*exp(c7*epsilon)*log(T*c8 + 1)` -> No epsilon**3.
33: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon) + c2*epsilon + c3*asinh(c4*epsilon) + c5*asinh(c6*epsilon*exp(T*c7))` -> No epsilon**3.
34: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + T**c3*c4*cos(c5*epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon` -> Has cos, no standalone sin. NO MATCH.
35: `T*c0*exp(c1*epsilon) + T*c2 + T*c3*epsilon**3 + T**c4*c5 + c6*epsilon**3 + c7` -> No sin.
36: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon) + c2*epsilon + c3*asinh(c4*epsilon) + c5*epsilon*exp(T*c6)` -> No epsilon**3.
37: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c1*epsilon**5 + c2*epsilon + c3*asinh(c4*epsilon) + c5*epsilon` -> No epsilon**3.
38: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**5 + c3*asinh(c4*epsilon)` -> No epsilon**3.
39: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c1*epsilon + c2*asinh(c3*epsilon) + c4*epsilon**4*(T*c5 + 1)` -> No epsilon**3.
40: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon) + T*c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon + c5*asinh(c6*epsilon)` -> No epsilon**3.
41: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon) + T*c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon + c4*asinh(c5*epsilon)` -> No epsilon**3.
42: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon) + c2*epsilon + c3*asinh(c4*epsilon) + c5*epsilon*(T + c6)` -> No epsilon**3.
43: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c1*epsilon + c2*sin(c3*epsilon)` -> No epsilon**3.
44: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c1*epsilon + c2*asinh(c3*epsilon) + c4*cos(c5*exp(c6*epsilon))` -> No epsilon**3.
45: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon) + c2*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**4*log(T*c5 + 1)` -> No standalone sin.
46: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + T*c3*sin(c4*epsilon + c5) + c6*epsilon + c7*asinh(c8*epsilon)` -> No epsilon**3.
47: `c0*log(c1*epsilon + 1)*cos(T*c2) + c3*sin(c4*epsilon) + c5*epsilon` -> No epsilon**3.
48: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c1*epsilon**3 + c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon**4*(T*c4 + 1)` -> No standalone sin.
49: `T*c0*sin(c1 + epsilon) + c2*epsilon + c3*asinh(c4*epsilon) + c5*epsilon + c6` -> No epsilon**3.
50: `T*c0*sin(c1 + epsilon) + c2*epsilon + c3*asinh(c4*epsilon) + c5` -> No epsilon**3.
51: `T*c0*sin(c1 + epsilon) + c2*epsilon + c3*asinh(c4*epsilon) + c5*log(c6*epsilon + 1)/epsilon` -> No epsilon**3.

Wait, let's double check Candidate 9 and 18.
Candidate 9: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*exp(T*c6)*sin(c7*epsilon + c8)`
If `c6 = 0`, `exp(T*c6) = 1`.
Then term is `c5*sin(c7*epsilon + c8)`.
Set `c7 = 1`, `c8 = 0` => `c5*sin(epsilon)`.
Set `c1 = 1`, `c2 = 0` => `T*c0*sin(epsilon)`.
Set `c4 = 0`.
Result: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c3*epsilon**3 + c5*sin(epsilon)`.
Matches GT exactly. So Candidate 9 is MATCH.

Candidate 18: `T*c0*sin(c1 + epsilon) + c2*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon + c4*sin(c5 + c6*epsilon)`
Set `c1 = 0` => `T*c0*sin(epsilon)`.
Set `c6 = 1`, `c5 = 0` => `c4*sin(epsilon)`.
Set `c3 = 0`.
Result: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c2*epsilon**3 + c4*sin(epsilon)`.
Matches GT exactly. So Candidate 18 is MATCH.

Are there any others?
Let's check Candidate 21 again: `(c0*epsilon + c1 + (T*c2 + c3)*(T*c4*sin(c5 + epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon))/(T*c2 + c3)`
This simplifies to `c0*epsilon/(T*c2+c3) + c1/(T*c2+c3) + T*c4*sin(c5+epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon`.
The `sin` term is multiplied by T. There is no standalone `sin(epsilon)` term. So it cannot match `C*sin(epsilon)`. Unless `c0*epsilon/(T*c2+c3)` or `c1/(T*c2+c3)` can produce `sin(epsilon)`? No, they are rational functions. So NO MATCH.

Candidate 24: `(c0*epsilon + c1 + (c2*epsilon + c3)*(T*c4*sin(c5 + epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon))/(c2*epsilon + c3)`
Simplifies to `c0*epsilon/(c2*epsilon+c3) + c1/(c2*epsilon+c3) + T*c4*sin(c5+epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon`.
Same issue. NO MATCH.

Candidate 27: `(T*c0 + c1 + (c2*epsilon + c3)*(T*c4*sin(c5 + epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon))/(c2*epsilon + c3)`
Simplifies to `T*c0/(c2*epsilon+c3) + c1/(c2*epsilon+c3) + T*c4*sin(c5+epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon`.
Same issue. NO MATCH.

Candidate 45: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon) + c2*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**4*log(T*c5 + 1)`
No standalone sin. NO MATCH.

Candidate 48: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c1*epsilon**3 + c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon**4*(T*c4 + 1)`
No standalone sin. NO MATCH.

Let's check Candidate 34 again: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + T**c3*c4*cos(c5*epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon`
Has `cos`, not `sin`. Can `cos` become `sin`? `cos(x) = sin(x + pi/2)`. But it's multiplied by `T**c3`. If `c3=0`, it's `c4*cos(c5*epsilon)`. This can be `C*sin(epsilon)` if `c5=1` and phase shift is handled? Wait, `cos(epsilon)` is not `sin(epsilon)`. They are linearly independent. So NO MATCH.

Let's check Candidate 17: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon + c4*asinh(c5*epsilon) + c6*sin(c7 + c8*epsilon)`
Has `T*sin(...)`, `sin(...)`, but no `epsilon**3`. NO MATCH.

Let's check Candidate 43: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c1*epsilon + c2*sin(c3*epsilon)`
No `epsilon**3`. NO MATCH.

So only Candidates 9 and 18 seem to match.

Wait, let's look at Candidate 1 again: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*cos(c6*exp(c7*epsilon))`
Could `c5*cos(c6*exp(c7*epsilon))` approximate `sin(epsilon)`? No, exact equivalence required.

Candidate 3: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*log(c6*exp(c7*epsilon) + 1)`
`log(c6*exp(c7*epsilon) + 1)` is softplus-like. Cannot be `sin(epsilon)`.

Candidate 6: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*exp(c6*sin(c7*epsilon + c8))`
`exp(sin(...))` cannot be `sin(epsilon)`.

Candidate 23: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*sin(c6*log(T*c7 + 1) + c8)`
`sin(log(T...))` depends on T. Cannot be standalone `sin(epsilon)`.

So 9 and 18 are the only ones.

Let's verify Candidate 9 carefully.
`T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon + c5*exp(T*c6)*sin(c7*epsilon + c8)`
Set `c6 = 0` => `exp(0) = 1`.
Set `c7 = 1`, `c8 = 0` => `sin(epsilon)`.
Set `c1 = 1`, `c2 = 0` => `sin(epsilon)`.
Set `c4 = 0`.
Expression: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c3*epsilon**3 + c5*sin(epsilon)`.
Matches `B*T*sin(epsilon) + A*epsilon**3 + C*sin(epsilon)`.
Yes.

Let's verify Candidate 18 carefully.
`T*c0*sin(c1 + epsilon) + c2*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon + c4*sin(c5 + c6*epsilon)`
Set `c1 = 0` => `sin(epsilon)`.
Set `c6 = 1`, `c5 = 0` => `sin(epsilon)`.
Set `c3 = 0`.
Expression: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c2*epsilon**3 + c4*sin(epsilon)`.
Matches.
Yes.

Are there any other candidates that might match via some identity?
What about Candidate 21? `(c0*epsilon + c1 + (T*c2 + c3)*(T*c4*sin(c5 + epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon))/(T*c2 + c3)`
If `c0=0, c1=0`, it simplifies to `T*c4*sin(c5+epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon`.
Still missing standalone `sin(epsilon)`.
Unless `c0*epsilon/(T*c2+c3)` can somehow produce `sin(epsilon)`? No.

What about Candidate 24? `(c0*epsilon + c1 + (c2*epsilon + c3)*(T*c4*sin(c5 + epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon))/(c2*epsilon + c3)`
Simplifies to `c0*epsilon/(c2*epsilon+c3) + c1/(c2*epsilon+c3) + T*c4*sin(c5+epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon`.

Simplifies to `T*c0/(c2*epsilon+c3) + c1/(c2*epsilon+c3) + T*c4*sin(c5+epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon`.
Missing standalone `sin(epsilon)`.

So only 9 and 18.

No standalone sin.

Candidate 48: `T*c0*sin(epsilon) + c1*epsilon**3 + c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon**4*(T*c4 + 1)`
No standalone sin.

Candidate 34: `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + T**c3*c4*cos(c5*epsilon) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon`
If `c3=0`, `T**0 = 1`. Then `c4*cos(c5*epsilon)`. Can `cos` match `sin`? No, they are linearly independent. Unless phase shift is allowed inside `cos`? `cos(x) = sin(x + pi/2)`. But the argument is `c5*epsilon`. We can't add a constant phase inside `cos` unless it's `cos(c5*epsilon + c_phase)`. Here it's just `cos(c5*epsilon)`. So it's strictly `cos`. Cannot match `sin`. NO MATCH.

Simplifies to `c0*epsilon/(T*c2+c3) + c1/(T*c2+c3) + T*c4*sin(c5*epsilon+c6) + c7*epsilon + c8*asinh(c9*epsilon)`.

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*(T - c3)*sin(epsilon)`
Substituting the given numerical constants (`c1=3.0`), we expand the GT into its fundamental basis functions:
`GT = A * epsilon**3 + B * T * sin(epsilon) + C * sin(epsilon)`
where `A = c0`, `B = c2`, and `C = -c2*c3`.
To match the GT, a candidate must be able to exactly reproduce three linearly independent terms across the continuous domain of `epsilon` and `T`:
1. `epsilon**3`
2. `T * sin(epsilon)`
3. `sin(epsilon)` (standalone, independent of `T`)

We will evaluate each candidate against these requirements.

---

### Candidate Analysis

- Contains `T*sin(...)` and `epsilon**3`.
- Lacks a standalone `sin(epsilon)` term. The `cos(...)` term cannot be transformed into `sin(epsilon)` exactly.
- Verdict: `[NO MATCH]`

**Candidate 2:** `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + c3*epsilon + c4*asinh(c5*epsilon) + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*epsilon) + 1)`

- Verdict: `[NO MATCH]`
